    • Non-contrast CT findings: hemorrhage, ischemic changes (ASPECTS)
    • Skull base: vascular grooves vs. fractures
    • Incidental soft tissue masses
  • 10
    Extracranial Soft Tissues
    • Neck soft tissues on cervical images
    • Lung apices, superior mediastinum
  • 11
    Last Checks
    • MIP reformats for stenosis
    • 3D VR for aneurysm and anatomy
    • Thin-slab MIP for small vessel assessment
    • Compare with prior CTA or MRA
MRI Brain MRI
Standard sequences: T1, T2, FLAIR, DWI/ADC, SWI or GRE, T1+C. Review in this sequence order. Additional: MRA, MRV, MRS, perfusion (ASL/DSC), functional MRI.
MRI Brain — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Stroke (DWI protocol), seizure (epilepsy protocol), headache, dementia, mass lesion, MS workup, infection, post-op
    • Prior MRI brain: date, field strength, sequences — load and compare directly
    • Gadolinium given: dose, timing, adverse reaction history
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences present: T1, T2, FLAIR, DWI/ADC, SWI/GRE, T1+C
    • 3T vs. 1.5T (note limitation)
    • Motion artifact, ghosting
    • Coverage: vertex to foramen magnum
  • 3
    T2 / FLAIR — Parenchymal Survey (Start Here)
    • White matter: periventricular lesions (MS — ovoid, juxtacortical, perpendicular to ventricles; Dawson fingers on sagittal FLAIR), subcortical, deep WM
    • Cortical signal: FLAIR cortical/gyral T2 brightness — meningitis, leptomeningeal carcinomatosis, seizure (post-ictal)
    • Leukoaraiosis: periventricular/subcortical confluent T2 bright — microvascular disease, Fazekas scale
    • Cerebral edema: sulcal effacement, loss of gray-white differentiation
    • Basal ganglia: T2 signal (hepatic encephalopathy — T1 bright; Wilson disease — T2 bright)
    • Brainstem: T2 bright pontine lesion (MS, glioma, osmotic demyelination)
    • Cerebellum: atrophy, T2 bright lesions (stroke territory, demyelination)
    • Ventricles: hydrocephalus (communicating — trans-ependymal T2 shine-through; non-communicating — mass at aqueduct or 4th)
    • Hippocampi: T2 signal, volume (hippocampal sclerosis)
    • Sulci: cortical atrophy pattern
  • 4
    DWI / ADC — Restricted Diffusion
    • Acute infarct: DWI bright + ADC dark = cytotoxic edema (onset <6 h — DWI positive before T2); vascular territory distribution
    • Subacute infarct: T2 shine-through on DWI with ADC pseudo-normalization (>1–2 weeks)
    • Abscess: rim-enhancing + DWI central restriction (high viscosity pus)
    • Epidermoid: DWI bright (vs. arachnoid cyst — DWI dark)
    • Dense cellularity: lymphoma, PNET/medulloblastoma, GBM central necrosis (variable)
    • Hypoxic-ischemic injury: bilateral cortical ribboning, basal ganglia restriction
    • Prion disease (CJD): cortical ribboning + basal ganglia/thalamus (pulvinar sign)
  • 5
    SWI / GRE — Blood Products & Susceptibility
    • Microhemorrhages: small punctate hypointense foci
    • Distribution: lobar (CAA — β-amyloid angiopathy), deep nuclei/infratentorial (hypertensive)
    • Cavernoma: popcorn morphology, complete hemosiderin ring
    • Calcifications: SWI — bilateral basal ganglia calcifications (Fahr, hypoparathyroidism)
    • Large blood products: subdural, epidural on SWI for staging (acute bright → subacute T1 bright → chronic dark on SWI)
    • Intraventricular blood: subtle blood products
  • 6
    T1 Pre-Contrast
    • T1-bright lesions: fat (lipoma, dermoid), blood products (met-hemoglobin 3–14 days), melanoma mets, proteinaceous cyst, calcification
    • Cortical laminar necrosis: T1-bright gyral pattern (subacute infarct)
    • Posterior pituitary bright spot: absent = central diabetes insipidus
    • Basal ganglia T1 brightness: hepatic failure, manganese, Pantothenate kinase, hypoxic-ischemic
    • White matter T1 dark: active demyelination, edema
  • 7
    T1 Post-Contrast — Enhancement Patterns
    • Blood-brain barrier breakdown: any enhancement = significant
    • Ring-enhancing: abscess (thick smooth ring, DWI central restriction) vs. GBM (thick irregular) vs. met (thin regular ring) — MAGIC DR mnemonic
    • Leptomeningeal enhancement: meningitis (bacterial — intense), leptomeningeal carcinomatosis, neurosarcoid
    • Nodular/solid: metastasis, meningioma (dural tail), lymphoma, medulloblastoma
    • Vascular enhancement: cortical vein thrombosis, AVM draining veins
    • Cranial nerve enhancement: CN VII (Bell palsy), CN V (perineural tumor spread, neurosarcoid)
    • Pituitary enhancement: microadenoma (hypointense relative to normal gland)
  • 8
    MRA (if included)
    • Circle of Willis: vessel caliber, flow-related signal
    • Aneurysm: focal outpouching; correlate with CTA if large
    • Stenosis or occlusion: flow void absence or signal reduction
    • Vertebrobasilar system: basilar artery patency
  • 9
    MRV (if included)
    • Dural venous sinus patency: SSS, transverse, sigmoid, straight, torcula
    • CVST: filling defect, delta sign on T1+C
    • Developmental variant: hypoplastic transverse sinus (left > right) — bilateral assessment
    • Cortical vein thrombosis: adjacent parenchymal injury
  • 10
    Extracranial Structures
    • Orbits: optic nerve signal, globe
    • Paranasal sinuses: fluid level, mucosal thickening, opacification (especially sphenoid near pituitary)
    • Mastoid air cells: opacification
    • Skull: lytic/sclerotic calvarial lesions, marrow signal
    • Scalp and subgaleal fat: masses
    • Cavernous sinus: asymmetry, thrombosis
  • 11
    Last Checks
    • Coronal and sagittal T1/FLAIR for corpus callosum lesions (MS), cerebellar tonsil position (Chiari)
    • Measure any lesion in 3 planes
    • Report total number of white matter lesions if MS protocol
    • Compare with all priors — new vs. old lesion critical distinction
MRI Brain — Seizure / Epilepsy Protocol MRI
Epilepsy protocol: thin-section coronal T2 and IR/FLAIR perpendicular to hippocampal axis, 3D T1 volumetric (MPRAGE), coronal FLAIR, DWI, T1+C (if new onset or focal). Goal: find structural epileptogenic substrate.
MRI Brain (Seizure) — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Seizure type: focal (temporal vs. extratemporal) vs. generalized
    • Duration of epilepsy: new-onset vs. refractory
    • Prior MRI (standard vs. epilepsy protocol), prior brain surgery, EEG lateralization
    • Family history: tuberous sclerosis, neurofibromatosis
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Epilepsy protocol sequences present: thin coronal T2 (3 mm), coronal FLAIR, 3D T1 volumetric (MPRAGE/BRAVO), DWI
    • Hippocampal-axis alignment of coronal sequences (oblique coronal perpendicular to long axis of hippocampus)
    • T1+C if first episode or focal neurologic deficit
  • 3
    Coronal T2 — Hippocampi (Primary Epilepsy Target)
    • Hippocampal sclerosis (MTS): unilateral T2 brightness, volume loss, loss of internal architecture (digitations)
    • Symmetry: compare CA1, CA3, CA4, subiculum
    • Hippocampal rotation (incomplete inversion): abnormal orientation — epilepsy association
    • Bilateral lesions (bilateral MTS or dual pathology)
  • 4
    T2 / FLAIR — Cortical Dysplasia & Other Substrates
    • Focal cortical dysplasia (FCD): T2/FLAIR bright cortex, blurred gray-white junction, transmantle sign (type II — extends to ventricle)
    • Cortical thickening and gyral abnormalities
    • Heterotopia: gray matter signal tissue in abnormal location (periventricular — smooth band, nodular; subcortical)
    • Tubers (tuberous sclerosis): T2 bright subcortical and cortical tubers, subependymal nodules
    • Cortical malformations: polymicrogyria, lissencephaly, schizencephaly
  • 5
    3D T1 Volumetric (MPRAGE)
    • Hippocampal volumetry: asymmetry ≥10–15% clinically significant
    • Gyral morphology: polymicrogyria (irregular sulcal pattern), pachygyria (simplified gyri)
    • Cortical thickness asymmetry: thinning (post-encephalitic, chronic ischemia)
    • Subcortical heterotopia: T1 dark gray matter bands
    • Cavernoma or other T1 bright lesion
  • 6
    DWI / ADC
    • Post-ictal restricted diffusion: DWI bright in ipsilateral cortex after prolonged seizure (pseudo-stroke — usually reversible)
    • Acute encephalitis: bilateral limbic T2/DWI changes
    • Acute ischemia if clinically indeterminate (stroke vs. seizure)
  • 7
    T1 Post-Contrast (if performed)
    • Low-grade glioma: subtle enhancement (FLAIR bright, ±enhancement)
    • DNET or ganglioglioma: typical temporal lobe; bubbly FLAIR, ±enhancement
    • Cavernoma: no enhancement; hemosiderin ring on SWI
    • Active encephalitis: cortical/meningeal enhancement
    • Hypothalamic hamartoma: no enhancement, isointense T1
  • 8
    SWI / GRE
    • Cavernoma: hallmark "popcorn" with hemosiderin ring (epileptogenic)
    • Calcifications in FCD type IIb, tubers
    • Small hemorrhagic lesion not visible on other sequences
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • Sagittal FLAIR: corpus callosum lesions (callosal dysgenesis, MS)
    • Cerebellar tonsil position: Chiari I (>5 mm below McRae line)
    • Compare with any prior standard brain MRI
    • If hippocampal sclerosis: lateralize (ipsilateral to EEG focus)
⚠ Negative epilepsy MRI does not exclude surgically remediable epilepsy — may need 7T or advanced post-processing.
MRI Orbits MRI
Fat saturation essential for optic nerve and post-contrast assessment. Coronal and axial planes required. DWI helpful for dense lesions. T1+C fat-sat in both planes.
MRI Orbits — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Vision loss, proptosis, diplopia, pain, pulsatile tinnitus, eyelid swelling, post-trauma
    • Prior imaging: CT orbits, prior MRI orbits
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: T2 fat-sat axial + coronal, T1, DWI, T1 fat-sat post-contrast axial + coronal
    • Coverage: apex of orbit through entire globe and periorbital structures
    • Fat saturation uniformity
  • 3
    T2 Fat-Sat — Soft Tissue Assessment (Start Here)
    • Optic nerve: T2 signal (optic neuritis — T2 bright, enlarged); perineural subarachnoid space enlargement (papilledema, NF-1, meningioma)
    • Globe: posterior coat thickening (uveal melanoma, choroidal effusion, retinal detachment — subretinal vs. choroidal fluid)
    • Extraocular muscles: thickening — thyroid eye disease (inferior > medial; apex sparing), myositis (tendinous insertion involvement)
    • Lacrimal gland: enlargement — sarcoid (most common cause of bilateral enlargement), lymphoma, Sjögren's, adenoid cystic Ca
    • Orbital fat: T2 stranding — cellulitis, pseudotumor, post-traumatic
    • Subperiosteal space: subperiosteal abscess (sinus origin), hematoma
    • Intraconal vs. extraconal space: location determines differential
  • 4
    DWI / ADC
    • Lymphoma: restricted diffusion (dense cellularity)
    • Retinoblastoma (children): dense, restricted diffusion
    • Schwannoma vs. meningioma: DWI usually unrestricted
    • Epidermoid: DWI bright (rare in orbit)
  • 5
    T1 Pre-Contrast
    • T1-bright lesions: fat (dermoid — anterior, superonasal), hemorrhage (blood cyst), melanoma (intrinsic T1 bright)
    • Normal structures: optic nerve, eye anatomy
    • Globe lesion morphology: choroidal melanoma (T1 bright, T2 variable)
  • 6
    T1 Fat-Sat Post-Contrast
    • Optic nerve enhancement: optic neuritis, optic nerve sheath meningioma (tram-track enhancement)
    • Extraocular muscle enhancement: active thyroid orbitopathy, myositis
    • Lacrimal gland enhancement: solid vs. cystic lesion
    • Orbital apex: compression of optic nerve at apex (surgical emergency)
    • Intracranial extension: cavernous sinus, optic chiasm, perineural spread along CN V1
    • Orbital wall masses: rhabdomyosarcoma (children), lymphoma, metastasis
  • 7
    Vascular Assessment
    • Cavernous sinus: symmetric enhancement, AV fistula (dilated superior ophthalmic vein)
    • Superior ophthalmic vein: dilation (orbital AV fistula, cavernous sinus thrombosis)
    • Orbital varix: enhancing dilated vein, increases with Valsalva
  • 8
    Intracranial Extension
    • Optic chiasm involvement: craniopharyngioma, pituitary macroadenoma, chiasmal glioma
    • Sphenoid wing meningioma: orbital extension
    • Skull base invasion: rhabdomyosarcoma, NPC extension
    • Cavernous sinus invasion: perineural spread
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • Sinuses: mucocele extending into orbit, orbital floor fracture (trauma)
    • Intracranial: brain parenchyma, visual pathway
    • Contralateral orbit: bilateral disease (lymphoma, sarcoid, TED, thyroid)
    • Children: retinoblastoma (calcification on CT), optic pathway glioma (NF-1)
MRI IAC / Posterior Fossa MRI
Key sequence: FIESTA/CISS/DRIVE thin-section T2 (0.8 mm isotropic) for nerve detail within IAC and CP angle cistern. Always bilateral and symmetrical comparison.
MRI IAC — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Unilateral SNHL, tinnitus, vertigo (Ménière's), facial nerve palsy, hemifacial spasm, CP angle mass
    • Prior MRI IAC, audiogram, and caloric testing results
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: FIESTA/CISS thin-section, T2 axial, T1, T1 fat-sat post-contrast
    • Coverage: bilateral IAC from fundus to brainstem; cerebellopontine angles
    • Fat saturation on T1+C (labyrinthine enhancement)
  • 3
    FIESTA / CISS / DRIVE — Cranial Nerve Detail (Start Here)
    • IAC contents: superior vestibular nerve (anterior superior), inferior vestibular nerve, cochlear nerve (anteroinferior), facial nerve (anterosuperior) — SAFE mnemonic
    • Cochlear nerve diameter: agenesis/hypoplasia (congenital SNHL workup)
    • Cochlea: modiolus, 2.5 turns, cochlear aperture patency
    • Semicircular canals: lateral, superior, posterior
    • Endolymphatic duct and sac: dilation (Ménière's)
    • CP angle cistern: CSF signal — mass (soft tissue displacing nerves vs. CSF-like signal = epidermoid or arachnoid cyst)
  • 4
    DWI / ADC
    • Epidermoid cyst: DWI bright (most important distinguishing feature from arachnoid cyst)
    • Cholesteatoma: DWI bright
    • Arachnoid cyst: DWI dark (CSF signal)
  • 5
    T1 Pre-Contrast
    • Labyrinthine hemorrhage: T1 bright in cochlea or vestibule (hemorrhagic labyrinthitis)
    • Lipoma: T1 bright fat along CN VII–VIII (rare, benign)
    • Posterior fossa hemorrhage: hyperacute blood on T1
  • 6
    T1 Fat-Sat Post-Contrast
    • Acoustic neuroma / vestibular schwannoma (VS): enhancing mass centered at IAC fundus or CP angle; "ice cream cone" shape; bilateral = NF-2
    • Facial nerve schwannoma: follows facial nerve canal (labyrinthine, geniculate, tympanic, mastoid segments)
    • Labyrinthine enhancement: acute labyrinthitis, viral (SNHL), suppurative labyrinthitis
    • Meningeal enhancement: meningitis, leptomeningeal carcinomatosis
    • Posterior fossa meningioma: dural-based, broad base, dural tail, CP angle
  • 7
    CP Angle Cistern
    • 3 most common CP angle masses: acoustic neuroma/VS (55%), meningioma (35%), epidermoid (5%)
    • Meningioma: obtuse angle with petrous bone, calcification, no IAC extension
    • Epidermoid: follows CSF on T1/T2, DWI bright, lobulated "cauliflower" shape
    • Arachnoid cyst: CSF signal on all sequences, mass effect
  • 8
    Brainstem & Cerebellum
    • Facial nerve nucleus: brainstem T2/FLAIR
    • Trigeminal nerve: neurovascular conflict (hemifacial spasm / trigeminal neuralgia — superior cerebellar artery or AICA contact)
    • Cerebellar hemisphere/tonsil: atrophy, lesion
    • Fourth ventricle: compression, displacement
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • Coronal views for superior semicircular canal dehiscence assessment
    • Compare IAC diameter bilaterally (>2 mm asymmetry = study posterior fossa)
    • Mastoid opacification on sequences
MRI Sella / Pituitary MRI
Thin-section (3 mm or less) coronal + sagittal T1 and T2. Dynamic coronal T1+C (early frames 20–30 s) essential for microadenoma detection. Coverage: cavernous sinuses to optic chiasm.
MRI Sella/Pituitary — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Hormone excess (Cushing's — ACTH; acromegaly — GH; hyperprolactinemia) vs. hormone deficiency (panhypopituitarism)
    • Visual field defects (bitemporal hemianopia — suprasellar extension, chiasm compression)
    • Headache; incidental on brain MRI; post-surgical assessment
    • Prior pituitary MRI, hormone levels, visual field testing
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: thin coronal T2, coronal + sagittal T1 pre-contrast, dynamic coronal T1+C (key), standard T1+C coronal + sagittal
    • Slice thickness ≤3 mm through sella
    • Coverage: clivus to suprasellar cistern; include cavernous sinuses
  • 3
    T2 — Pituitary Anatomy & Lesion Signal
    • Pituitary gland size: height — normal ≤8 mm women, ≤6 mm men (physiologic enlargement in pregnancy up to 12 mm)
    • Gland shape: symmetric convex vs. asymmetric bulge (microadenoma side)
    • Stalk: midline vs. deviation (deviation toward normal side suggests adenoma on opposite side)
    • Optic chiasm: position (prefixed, normal, postfixed); elevation or compression
    • Hypothalamus: mass, hamartoma (isointense T2, no enhancement)
    • Cavernous sinuses: T2 signal, symmetric enhancement
    • T2 signal of lesion: bright = Rathke cleft cyst (unilocular, follows CSF), craniopharyngioma (heterogeneous, cystic), cystic adenoma
  • 4
    T1 Pre-Contrast — Fat & Bright Signal
    • Posterior pituitary bright spot (neurohypophysis): normally T1 bright — absence = central DI or infiltration
    • T1 bright lesion: craniopharyngioma (cholesterol-rich cyst), Rathke cleft cyst (protein-rich), hemorrhagic adenoma (apoplexy)
    • Fat: dermoid, lipoma
  • 5
    Dynamic T1+C (Coronal, Early Frames) — Microadenoma Detection
    • Normal pituitary enhances quickly and uniformly
    • Microadenoma (<10 mm): hypointense relative to brightly enhancing normal gland in early frames
    • Stalk wash-in: normal stalk enhancement on early frames
    • Later frames: adenoma may fill in (isointense) — early timing critical
    • ACTH-producing microadenoma (Cushing's): often very small (<6 mm), may require inferior petrosal sinus sampling if not seen
  • 6
    Standard T1+C (Coronal + Sagittal) — Macroadenoma & Extent
    • Macroadenoma (≥10 mm): solid enhancement, may be heterogeneous (necrosis, hemorrhage)
    • Suprasellar extension: degree of chiasm elevation/compression (bitemporal hemianopia threshold)
    • Cavernous sinus invasion: Knosp grading (0–4); grade ≥3 = true invasion, not surgically curable
    • Sphenoid sinus extension: surgical route planning (transsphenoidal)
    • Apoplexy: heterogeneous enhancement, hemorrhage or infarction within macroadenoma
  • 7
    Parasellar & Suprasellar Lesions (Differential)
    • Craniopharyngioma: suprasellar, calcified (adamantinomatous type), cystic, cholesterol crystals
    • Meningioma: parasellar or tuberculum sellae; homogeneous enhancement, dural tail, calcification
    • Rathke cleft cyst: intrasellar/suprasellar, T2 bright, no enhancement
    • Pituitary hyperplasia: diffuse gland enlargement (hypothyroidism, pregnancy, puberty) — diagnosis of exclusion
    • Aneurysm: pulsatile, flow void on T2, risk of rupture — CTA or MRA to confirm
  • 8
    Optic Pathway
    • Chiasm: compression, signal change (T2 bright = edema/ischemia)
    • Optic nerves: sheath thickening (meningioma)
    • Optic tracts: compression leading to homonymous hemianopia
  • 9
    Extratarget
    • Sphenoid sinus: mucocele, inflammatory disease (can elevate pituitary floor)
    • Clivus: chordoma (T2 very bright, destructive)
    • Temporal lobes: herniation risk with large macroadenoma
  • 10
    Last Checks
    • Measure adenoma in 3 dimensions
    • Note Knosp grade for macroadenoma
    • Note stalk position
    • Compare with prior pituitary MRI carefully for interval change in size
MRI Soft Tissue Neck MRI
Standard: T1, T2 fat-sat or STIR, DWI, T1 fat-sat post-contrast. Axial primary plane + sagittal/coronal for longitudinal extent. Coverage: skull base to thoracic inlet/clavicles.
MRI Soft Tissue Neck — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Neck mass: duration, growth, pain, voice changes, dysphagia, B symptoms
    • Prior surgery or radiation (post-treatment changes, recurrence vs. fibrosis)
    • Primary SCC of pharynx/larynx — staging vs. nodes only
    • Prior CT or PET-CT for comparison; gadolinium planned
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: T2 fat-sat axial + coronal, STIR sagittal, DWI, T1 axial, T1 fat-sat post-contrast axial + coronal
    • Coverage: skull base to clavicles
    • Fat saturation uniformity, motion artifact, metallic artifact from dental hardware
  • 3
    T2 Fat-Sat / STIR — Tissue Characterization (Start Here)
    • Primary tumor signal: T2 intermediate-to-bright (SCC), T2 bright (minor salivary gland mucoepidermoid)
    • Nodal signal: necrotic nodes (T2 bright center, thick walls), extranodal extension (ill-defined margins into fat)
    • Thyroid gland: T2 signal — heterogeneous nodular gland; cysts (T2 very bright)
    • Salivary glands: parotid (predominantly fatty T2), submandibular, sublingual masses
    • Pharyngeal walls: thickness, symmetry, mucosal asymmetry
    • Larynx: aryepiglottic folds, glottis — T2 signal of cartilages (T2 bright = edema; after radiation — expected change vs. recurrence)
    • Pre/paravertebral muscles: edema (T2 bright) — direct invasion vs. reactive
    • Bone marrow (clivus, C-spine): T2 signal — normal fatty marrow vs. T2 bright edema
  • 4
    DWI / ADC
    • Primary tumor: restricted diffusion correlates with tumor cellularity; SCC is hypointense on ADC
    • Metastatic nodes: restricted diffusion + necrosis (central T2 bright + rim enhancement)
    • Lymphoma: markedly restricted diffusion (high cellularity)
    • Post-treatment: scar (no restriction) vs. recurrence (restriction)
  • 5
    T1 — Fat Planes & Marrow
    • Fat planes: preserved = no invasion; obliterated fat = suspect invasion of adjacent structure
    • Parapharyngeal fat (key landmark): displaced toward mass (indicates origin; intrinsic parapharyngeal mass = fat centered)
    • Bone marrow signal: vertebral body fat = normal; T1 dark = metastatic replacement, infection
    • Carotid arterial signal: flow void = patent; T1 bright thrombus
  • 6
    T1 Fat-Sat Post-Contrast
    • Primary tumor enhancement: solid, heterogeneous; extent of enhancement defines gross tumor volume (GTV) for radiation planning
    • Perineural spread (critical finding): enlargement and enhancement of foramina (foramen ovale CN V3, stylomastoid CN VII, jugular foramen CN IX/X/XI), retrograde tracking along nerve
    • Nodal enhancement: necrotic core (dark) + enhancing rim = necrotic nodal metastasis
    • Vascular invasion: carotid encasement (≥270° contact = unresectable)
    • Post-treatment: mucosal enhancement suggests active disease vs. mucosal/submucosal fibrosis (T1 dark, no enhancement)
  • 7
    Lymph Node Levels
    • Level I: submandibular, submental
    • Level II: upper jugular (IIA — anterior to IJV; IIB — posterior)
    • Level III: mid-jugular
    • Level IV: lower jugular
    • Level V: posterior cervical triangle
    • Level VI: anterior/central compartment (paratracheal, prelaryngeal, pretracheal)
    • Retropharyngeal nodes: lateral ≥8 mm SAX, medial (Rouvière) ≥5 mm
    • Note: size, necrosis, extranodal extension (ENE) for each suspicious node
  • 8
    Deep Neck Spaces
    • Parapharyngeal: fat preserved/displaced
    • Masticator: pterygoid muscle invasion, mandible cortex
    • Retropharyngeal/danger spaces: abscess, mass — potential mediastinal extension
    • Carotid space: ICA/IJV, paraganglioma (splaying ICA/ECA), schwannoma
    • Visceral space: thyroid, parathyroid, trachea, esophagus
  • 9
    Skull Base & Intracranial
    • Foramina: ovale, spinosum, rotundum, stylomastoid — perineural spread tracking
    • Clivus, petrous apex, cavernous sinus invasion
    • Intracranial extension: subdural, parenchymal
    • Nasopharynx apex: Rosenmuller fossa asymmetry, NPC extension
  • 10
    Extratarget
    • Lung apices: metastasis, lymphoma
    • Thyroid: incidental nodules, substernal extension
    • Cervical spine: marrow signal
    • Superior mediastinum: lymphadenopathy
  • 11
    Last Checks
    • Sagittal for longitudinal extent and retropharyngeal space
    • Coronal for paramedian structures, skull base foramina
    • Measure primary tumor in 3D
    • Nodal levels: complete mapping for staging
    • Assign T, N stage if oncologic study
MRI Cervical Spine MRI
Standard: sagittal T2, sagittal STIR (or fat-sat T2), sagittal T1, axial T2 (GRE/MEDIC in trauma for cord detail). T1+C if infection, tumor, or post-surgical. Cover C1–T1 (or T2).
MRI Cervical Spine — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Myelopathy (hand clumsiness, gait, bowel/bladder), radiculopathy (dermatomal pain/numbness/weakness), trauma, known malignancy, inflammatory arthritis
    • Prior MRI cervical spine: compare level-by-level
    • Gadolinium given? (infection, tumor, demyelination, post-op)
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: sagittal T2, sagittal STIR or fat-sat T2, sagittal T1, axial T2 or GRE
    • T1+C sagittal and axial if indicated
    • Coverage: brainstem/craniocervical junction through C7–T1
  • 3
    Sagittal T2 — Primary Survey (Start Here)
    • Spinal cord signal: T2 bright intramedullary lesion — myelopathy (chronic degenerative — central T2 bright behind disk), demyelination (MS plaque — short-segment, eccentric, peripheral), tumor (ependymoma — central with hemosiderin caps; astrocytoma — fusiform), syrinx (T2 bright fluid-filled cavity within cord)
    • Cord diameter: focal thinning = chronic myelomalacia; swelling = acute cord injury or tumor
    • Disk herniations: central, paracentral, foraminal, far-lateral; disc signal (dark = degenerated)
    • Vertebral body alignment: anterolisthesis/retrolisthesis
    • Canal diameter: anterior-posterior; ligamentum flavum buckling posterior
  • 4
    Sagittal STIR — Edema-Sensitive Survey
    • Vertebral body marrow edema: T2 bright (acute fracture vs. metastasis vs. infection — Modic 1 change)
    • Disk endplate signal: Modic type 1 (T2 bright = active degeneration), type 2 (T1 bright fat), type 3 (T1/T2 dark = sclerosis)
    • Paraspinal soft tissue edema: infection, ligamentous injury, post-traumatic
    • Posterior ligamentous complex: STIR bright = ligamentous injury (trauma)
  • 5
    Sagittal T1 — Marrow & Fat Anatomy
    • Normal vertebral marrow: T1 bright (fat-containing)
    • Pathologic marrow replacement: T1 dark = metastasis, lymphoma, myeloma, infection, edema (low specificity on T1 alone — needs STIR correlation)
    • Fatty Schmorl nodes and end-plate changes (T1 bright = Modic 2)
    • Foraminal fat: T1 bright preservation = no foraminal stenosis; obliteration = stenosis
  • 6
    Axial T2 / GRE — Level-by-Level Canal Assessment
    • Central canal: AP diameter; spinal cord compression grading (Kang/modified JOA for clinical significance)
    • Cord morphology: central gray butterfly, size, signal per level
    • Disk herniation: type (central, subarticular, foraminal, extraforaminal), contact with nerve root, cord contact
    • Uncovertebral joint osteophytes: lateral canal/foraminal narrowing
    • Ligamentum flavum: hypertrophy = posterior canal compromise
    • Facet joints: arthropathy, hypertrophic changes
  • 7
    T1 Post-Contrast (if performed)
    • Cord enhancement: demyelination (active MS plaque enhances with Gd — ring or solid), ependymoma/astrocytoma
    • Epidural enhancement: epidural abscess (rim-enhancing fluid collection), granulation tissue (post-surgical)
    • Disk/endplate enhancement: diskitis-osteomyelitis (end plates + disk)
    • Meningeal enhancement: leptomeningeal metastases, arachnoiditis
    • Paraspinal/pre/retro-vertebral enhancement: phlegmon vs. abscess
  • 8
    Extratarget Structures
    • Posterior fossa and craniocervical junction: Chiari malformation (tonsils >5 mm below McRae line), os odontoideum, pannus (RA)
    • Lung apices: Pancoast tumor (correlate with radiculopathy)
    • Thyroid and prevertebral soft tissues
    • Vertebral arteries in foramina transversaria (flow voids)
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • Note spinal cord level of injury/lesion
    • Measure any disk herniation or canal compromise in mm
    • Ensure C7-T1 junction included
    • Report cord signal change (myelopathy) prominently — impacts surgical decision
⚠ Myelopathy: T2 bright cord signal + clinical symptoms = surgical emergency. Report cord compression grade at each relevant level.
MRI Thoracic Spine MRI
Sagittal T2 is the key sequence. Conus medullaris at T12–L1 is critical. T1+C for cord lesions, metastases, infection. Axial T2 through levels of cord signal change or suspected disk herniation.
MRI Thoracic Spine — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Myelopathy (bilateral leg weakness, gait, bowel/bladder — thoracic cord lesion until proven otherwise), back pain with cord signs, known malignancy/staging, scoliosis MRI, suspected infection/demyelination
    • Prior MRI thoracic spine
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: sagittal T2, sagittal STIR, sagittal T1, axial T2 (at levels of interest)
    • Coverage: cervicothoracic junction through conus (T12–L1)
    • T1+C if cord signal change, infection, or tumor
  • 3
    Sagittal T2 — Primary Survey
    • Spinal cord signal: entire length of thoracic cord; T2 bright intramedullary signal
    • Cord lesion characterization: ependymoma (central, hemosiderin caps), astrocytoma (fusiform, ill-defined), MS plaques (short-segment, ≤2 vertebral segments, peripheral), NMO (>3 segments, central — holospinal), syringomyelia (fluid cavity)
    • Conus position: normal T12–L1; low-lying conus = tethered cord
    • Disk herniations: less common in thoracic spine; calcified disks
    • Vertebral body alignment and height
    • Canal diameter
  • 4
    Sagittal STIR — Bone Marrow & Soft Tissue Edema
    • Vertebral body edema: metastases (T2/STIR bright, round vs. confluent), acute compression fracture (T2 bright = edema), infection
    • Paraspinal signal: abscess (T2 bright collection), inflammatory change
    • Posterior elements: stress reactions, fracture edema
    • Ligamentous injury (trauma): posterior ligamentous complex T2/STIR bright
  • 5
    Sagittal T1 — Marrow Signal
    • Normal marrow: T1 bright fat throughout
    • Metastatic replacement: T1 dark lesions (focal or diffuse — marrow replacement pattern)
    • Hemangioma: T1 bright "corduroy" or stippled pattern (fat-containing trabeculae)
    • Degenerative changes: Schmorl nodes, end plate irregularity
    • Fracture morphology: T1 signal within vertebral body — acute (T1 dark edema) vs. chronic (T1 bright fat)
  • 6
    Axial T2 — Level-by-Level (Levels of Interest)
    • Cord morphology and diameter
    • Disk herniation morphology and cord contact
    • Canal diameter
    • Epidural abnormality: abscess, hematoma, metastasis
  • 7
    T1 Post-Contrast (if performed)
    • Cord enhancement: active demyelination (MS), ependymoma enhancement, intramedullary abscess (rare)
    • Leptomeningeal enhancement: carcinomatosis, TB, CMV (HIV)
    • Epidural enhancement: metastatic disease, abscess, post-surgical granulation tissue
    • Vertebral/disk enhancement: diskitis-osteomyelitis (end plates + disk)
  • 8
    Extratarget Structures
    • Visualized lungs and pleura: pleural effusion, consolidation, mediastinal mass
    • Aorta and great vessels: thoracic aortic aneurysm, atherosclerosis
    • Heart: pericardial effusion
    • Liver dome, spleen, adrenals on inferior images
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • Count vertebral levels from cervicothoracic junction (T1)
    • Note cord signal change level precisely
    • Measure any epidural collection or canal compromise
    • Conus position: report if low (below L2 in adults = tethered cord)
⚠ Myelopathy localizing to thoracic cord: T2 signal ≥3 segments = NMO spectrum (AQP4/MOG); <3 segments eccentric = MS; central enhancement = ependymoma.
MRI Lumbar Spine MRI
Most common MRI study. Sagittal T2 is workhorse. Axial T2 at every disk level is mandatory. STIR for edema. T1+C for infection, tumor, post-operative. Cover L1–S1 (include T12 and sacrum).
MRI Lumbar Spine — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Low back pain, radiculopathy (dermatomal pattern, which level?), neurogenic claudication, known malignancy, cauda equina syndrome, prior spine surgery
    • Prior MRI lumbar spine — compare level by level
    • Gadolinium given? (post-op: scar vs. recurrent disk; infection; tumor)
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: sagittal T2, sagittal STIR or fat-sat T2, sagittal T1, axial T2 at each disk level
    • T1+C sagittal + axial if post-surgical or infection
    • Coverage: T12/L1 junction through sacrum including S1 nerve roots
  • 3
    Sagittal T2 — Primary Survey (Start Here)
    • Disk signal: T2 bright (hydrated) vs. dark (desiccated/degenerated); note each level
    • Disk height: reduced = degeneration or infection (diskitis — rapid height loss + end plate destruction)
    • Posterior disk morphology: central vs. paracentral protrusion/extrusion (size, direction, relationship to level)
    • Vertebral body alignment: spondylolisthesis (grade I–IV; antero- vs. retro-)
    • Spinal canal diameter: AP diameter; central stenosis
    • Conus and cauda equina: conus at T12–L1; tethered cord (low conus + fatty filum)
    • Thecal sac: conus signal, cauda equina clumping (arachnoiditis)
  • 4
    Sagittal STIR — Marrow Edema & Soft Tissue
    • Vertebral body edema: acute fractures (T2/STIR bright), metastases (multiple lesions), infection (end plate STIR bright)
    • Modic type 1 changes: T2 bright end plates (active degeneration/inflammation) — look for infection correlation
    • Posterior elements: pars stress reaction (STIR bright), facet joint edema
    • Paraspinal muscles: edema pattern
  • 5
    Sagittal T1 — Marrow & Anatomy
    • Normal marrow: T1 bright throughout
    • Metastatic or myelomatous replacement: T1 dark lesion
    • Hemangioma: T1 bright (fat-containing)
    • Fatty end plates (Modic 2): T1 bright bilateral end plate signal
    • Schmorl nodes: T1 dark if active; T1 bright if chronic fat-containing
    • Foraminal fat preservation: bilaterally; obliteration = foraminal stenosis
  • 6
    Axial T2 — Level-by-Level (L1–2 through L5–S1)
    • Each disk level in sequence
    • Central canal diameter (AP) — critical stenosis <10 mm
    • Lateral recess: nerve root position — open vs. compressed (recess <3 mm = likely stenosis)
    • Foraminal patency: fat around exiting nerve root (obliterated = stenosis)
    • Disk morphology: focal vs. broad-based (>25%); herniation type (protrusion, extrusion, sequestration)
    • Ligamentum flavum: hypertrophy (posterior compression)
    • Facet joints: arthropathy, effusion, synovial cyst (intraspinal extension)
  • 7
    T1 Post-Contrast (if performed)
    • Post-surgical scar vs. recurrent disk herniation: scar enhances peripherally and homogeneously; recurrent disk — peripheral rim enhancement
    • Epidural abscess: rim-enhancing posterior or anterior epidural collection
    • Diskitis-osteomyelitis: end plate and disk enhancement + STIR bright
    • Tumor/metastasis: vertebral body and epidural extension enhancement
    • Cauda equina nerve root enhancement: Guillain-Barré, AIDP, CMT, leptomeningeal carcinomatosis
  • 8
    Sacrum & Pelvis
    • Sacral marrow signal: insufficiency fractures (STIR bright H-pattern), metastases
    • SI joints: erosion, sclerosis, ankylosis (sacroiliitis — bilateral vs. unilateral)
    • Pelvic floor muscles visible on lower sections
  • 9
    Extratarget Structures
    • Aorta and iliac vessels on axial: AAA, atherosclerosis
    • Kidneys: hydronephrosis, renal mass
    • Uterus/ovaries or prostate on lower sections
    • Pelvic lymph nodes
    • Presacral mass
  • 10
    Last Checks
    • For each level: herniation type, nerve root contact, lateral recess grade, foraminal grade
    • Note dominant level correlating with clinical radiculopathy
    • Count from L5–S1 upward (sacrum is reference)
    • Note transitional anatomy: Bertolotti syndrome (partial sacralization L5)
⚠ Cauda equina syndrome: central disk herniation + urinary retention/saddle anesthesia = surgical emergency. Report directly to clinical team.
MRI Total Spine MRI
Sagittal T2 is gold standard for screening. Sagittal T1 or STIR at each region. Add axials at any abnormal level. T1+C for metastases, infection, leptomeningeal disease.
MRI Total Spine — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Known malignancy (metastatic survey), myelopathy (localize level), demyelination (MS/NMO total cord), tethered cord, vascular malformation, systemic infection
    • Prior total spine MRI — compare all three regions
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: sagittal T2 cervical + thoracic + lumbar, sagittal T1 or STIR at each region, axials at levels of concern
    • T1+C if tumor, infection, or leptomeningeal indication
    • Coverage: brainstem/craniocervical junction through sacrum; no gaps between regional studies
  • 3
    Sagittal T2 — Cervical Region
    • Cord signal throughout cervical cord; focal T2 bright lesion, syrinx
    • Disk herniations and cord compression levels
    • Craniocervical junction: Chiari, atlantoaxial instability
  • 4
    Sagittal T2 — Thoracic Region
    • Cord signal; conus position and signal
    • Intradural extramedullary lesions: meningioma (broad dural base, iso-T2), schwannoma (T2 bright, dumbbell), myxopapillary ependymoma (filum)
    • Vertebral body signal: metastases, fractures
    • Disk disease less common but thoracic disk herniation can cause myelopathy
  • 5
    Sagittal T2 — Lumbar Region
    • Cauda equina: nerve root clumping (arachnoiditis), leptomeningeal enhancement
    • Conus: tethered cord, lipoma of filum
    • Disk disease, vertebral metastases
    • Sacrum and sacral nerve roots
  • 6
    STIR — All Three Regions
    • Marrow edema pattern: contiguous (infection, trauma) vs. skip lesions (metastases — classic skip distribution)
    • Paravertebral edema: abscess, tumor extension
    • Ligamentous injury: posterior ligament complex
  • 7
    T1 — All Three Regions
    • Marrow signal uniformity: T1 dark = pathologic replacement at any level
    • Vertebral hemangiomas: T1 bright (benign, common)
    • Heterogeneous marrow: myeloma, lymphoma
    • Normal fat in sacrum and pelvis visible inferiorly
  • 8
    Axials at Levels of Concern
    • Cord morphology, compression grade
    • Epidural extension of tumor or abscess
    • Canal diameter and intraspinal lesion characterization
  • 9
    T1 Post-Contrast (if performed)
    • Leptomeningeal carcinomatosis: extensive nerve root and cord surface enhancement
    • Intradural extramedullary tumors: intense enhancement (meningioma, schwannoma)
    • Intramedullary lesions: ependymoma (homogeneous enhancement, central), astrocytoma (heterogeneous)
    • Vertebral and epidural metastases: avid enhancement
    • Diskitis-osteomyelitis: end plate + disk enhancement pattern
  • 10
    Extratarget Structures
    • Posterior fossa on cervical images
    • Thoracic organs: mediastinum, lungs, heart
    • Abdominal organs on lower thoracic/upper lumbar images
    • Pelvic organs on lumbar/sacral images
  • 11
    Last Checks
    • Localize any cord signal change to precise vertebral level
    • Epidural cord compression grade at each involved level (ESCC scale for metastases: 0–3)
    • Count metastatic foci: total number, highest level of compression
    • Compare with prior total spine if metastatic disease
⚠ Epidural spinal cord compression (ESCC grade 2–3): contact neurologist/neurosurgeon immediately. IV dexamethasone if cord compression with deficit.
MSK X-Ray — General Approach XR
A B C D SAlignment · Bone density & cortex · Cartilage (joint space) · Density/soft tissue · Soft tissue
MSK X-Ray — General Approach (ABCDS)
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Mechanism: acute trauma vs. chronic/atraumatic pain
    • Age: epiphyseal vs. metaphyseal vs. diaphyseal lesion differential; pediatric growth plates
    • Prior XRs for comparison — essential for lesion characterization
  • 2
    Adequacy & Views
    • Minimum two perpendicular views (AP + lateral)
    • Special views as needed (oblique, stress, weight-bearing)
    • Include joint above and below for long bone injuries
  • 3
    Alignment
    • Bone axes: angulation, rotation, translation
    • Joint alignment: subluxation vs. dislocation
    • Joint space width: symmetric vs. asymmetric narrowing
  • 4
    Bone Density & Cortex
    • Overall density: osteoporosis (diffuse), metastasis, Paget
    • Cortical integrity: fracture line continuity, cortical disruption
    • Trabecular pattern: disruption in occult fracture (scaphoid, femoral neck)
  • 5
    Cartilage / Joint Space
    • Narrowing: uniform (RA, infection) vs. asymmetric (OA — weight-bearing side)
    • Subchondral sclerosis and cysts: OA
    • Widening: effusion, infection, acromegaly
  • 6
    Lesion Analysis (if applicable)
    • Zone of transition: narrow (benign/geographic) vs. wide (aggressive/permeative — malignant)
    • Periosteal reaction: solid (benign), lamellated (Codman triangle), sunburst (Ewing, osteosarcoma)
    • Matrix: osteoid (fluffy/cloud-like), chondroid (rings/arcs), fibrous (ground-glass)
    • Location: epiphysis (chondroblastoma, GCT), metaphysis (osteosarcoma, NOF), diaphysis (Ewing, ABC)
  • 7
    Soft Tissues
    • Swelling: joint (effusion vs. periarticular) vs. soft tissue mass
    • Calcifications: myositis ossificans, CPPD, gout tophi, tumoral calcinosis
    • Periarticular fat pads: displaced = effusion (posterior elbow, anterior ankle)
  • 8
    Compare Bilaterally (Pediatric / Epiphyseal)
    • Growth plates: symmetric (normal) vs. asymmetric widening/sclerosis
    • Epiphyseal ossification centers: age-appropriate development
Shoulder X-Ray XR
Shoulder X-Ray — Systematic Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Trauma (FOOSH, direct blow, overhead fall), pain, instability, rotator cuff, post-op
  • 2
    Views
    • AP internal/external rotation, Y-scapular, axillary
    • Grashey (true AP) for glenohumeral joint; Zanca for AC joint
  • 3
    Alignment & Joint Position
    • Glenohumeral: humeral head centered on glenoid
    • Anterior dislocation: subcoracoid position (loss of overlap)
    • Posterior dislocation: lightbulb sign (fixed internal rotation); check axillary view
    • AC joint dislocation: Rockwood grade I–VI (CC distance normal ≤13 mm)
  • 4
    Humeral Head
    • Hill-Sachs: posterolateral head compression fracture (anterior dislocation)
    • Reverse Hill-Sachs (McLaughlin): anteromedial head (posterior dislocation)
    • Greater tuberosity fracture: rotator cuff avulsion
    • Surgical neck fracture: Neer classification
  • 5
    Glenoid & Scapula
    • Bony Bankart: anteroinferior glenoid rim fracture
    • Scapular body/neck fracture; coracoid fracture
    • Floating shoulder: clavicle + scapular neck fracture
  • 6
    Clavicle
    • Midshaft (80%): shortening, displacement
    • Distal clavicle: Neer type I (stable) vs. II (CC ligament disrupted — unstable)
  • 7
    Acromion & Subacromial Space
    • Subacromial space ≥6 mm; <6 mm = impingement risk
    • Acromial morphology: type I (flat), II (curved), III (hooked — impingement)
    • Os acromiale: unfused anterior acromion
  • 8
    Calcifications
    • Calcific tendinitis: dense calcification in supraspinatus (most common)
  • 9
    Bone Lesions
    • Proximal humerus: metastases, GCT, UBC, ABC
    • Enchondroma in distal clavicle
  • 10
    Soft Tissues
    • Swelling, calcifications, foreign body
Elbow X-Ray XR
Elbow X-Ray — Systematic Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • FOOSH (radial head), varus/valgus stress, pediatric (NV status critical), locking
  • 2
    Views
    • AP (forearm supinated) + lateral (90° flexion)
    • Radial head-capitellum view for radial head fracture; axial for olecranon
  • 3
    Alignment
    • Radiocapitellar line: must bisect capitellum on all views (disruption = radial head dislocation)
    • Anterior humeral line: should intersect middle third of capitellum (posterior dislocation if anterior)
    • Carrying angle: normal valgus 10–15°
  • 4
    Fat Pads
    • Anterior fat pad: normal thin sail; elevated = effusion
    • Posterior fat pad: always pathologic = effusion (occult fracture until proven otherwise)
  • 5
    Distal Humerus
    • Lateral condyle fracture (pediatric — Milch/Salter-Harris)
    • Medial epicondyle fracture (check for entrapment in joint after dislocation)
    • Supracondylar fracture (pediatric — Gartland I–III; anterior humeral line)
    • Capitellum OCD (anterolateral); Kocher-Lorenz coronal shear fracture
  • 6
    Radial Head & Neck
    • Radial head fracture: Mason I–IV
    • Rule out Monteggia: ulnar fracture + radial head dislocation
  • 7
    Olecranon & Ulna
    • Olecranon fracture: displaced vs. non-displaced
    • Coronoid fracture: Regan-Morrey I–III; terrible triad = coronoid + radial head + LCL
    • Monteggia: ulnar fracture + radial head dislocation
  • 8
    Elbow Dislocation
    • Direction: posterior (most common)
    • Terrible triad: posterior dislocation + radial head + coronoid
  • 9
    Bone Lesions & Soft Tissues
    • Cortical lesions, periosteal reaction
    • Myositis ossificans, loose bodies in olecranon fossa
  • 10
    Pediatric Growth Plates (CRITOE)
    • Capitellum(1y) → Radial head(3y) → Internal epicondyle(5y) → Trochlea(7y) → Olecranon(9y) → External epicondyle(11y)
    • Missing internal epicondyle after dislocation = may be trapped in joint
⚠ Posterior fat pad always pathologic. Pediatric: check CRITOE centers.
Wrist / Hand X-Ray XR
Wrist/Hand X-Ray — Systematic Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • FOOSH, snuffbox tenderness, dorsal vs. volar pain, finger mechanism
  • 2
    Views
    • Wrist: PA, lateral, oblique; scaphoid: ulnar deviation + PA
    • Hand: PA, oblique, lateral; fingers: dedicated PA + lateral
  • 3
    Carpal Alignment (Lateral)
    • Gilula arcs I–III: smooth = normal; disruption = instability
    • Lateral: colinear radius–lunate–capitate
    • SL angle 30–60°; RL angle <15°; DISI: SL >70°
  • 4
    Scaphoid
    • Waist (70%), proximal pole (20%), distal (10%)
    • All 4 views for fracture line
    • Humpback deformity on lateral >35° = unstable
    • Proximal pole sclerosis = AVN
  • 5
    Other Carpal Bones
    • Lunate: Kienböck disease (T1 dark on MRI; sclerosis/collapse on XR)
    • Triquetrum: dorsal chip fracture (lateral view)
    • Hamate: hook fracture (carpal tunnel view)
    • Perilunate dislocation: capitate not overlying lunate
  • 6
    Distal Radius & Ulna
    • Colles (dorsal angulation), Smith (volar), Barton (intra-articular shear), die-punch
    • DRUJ: radial inclination <15° or ulnar variance >+2 mm
    • Ulnar styloid base fracture = TFCC disruption
  • 7
    Metacarpals & Phalanges
    • Boxer fracture: 5th MC neck (acceptable angulation ≤40°)
    • Bennett (intra-articular 1st CMC), Rolando (comminuted Bennett)
    • Mallet finger: distal phalanx extensor avulsion
    • Gamekeeper's thumb: ulnar collateral ligament avulsion
  • 8
    Joints
    • RA: uniform narrowing, periarticular osteoporosis, ulnar drift, swan-neck/boutonnière
    • Gout: eccentric erosions with overhanging edge, preserved joint space
    • OA: DIP and 1st CMC
  • 9
    Bone Density & Soft Tissues
    • Periarticular osteopenia (early RA)
    • CPPD calcification: triangular fibrocartilage, SL ligament
  • 10
    Pediatric Growth Plates
    • Distal radius Salter-Harris II most common after FOOSH
    • Differentiate physeal lines from acute fractures
⚠ Scaphoid tenderness + normal XR = treat as fracture until MRI confirmed.
Hip / Pelvis X-Ray XR
Hip/Pelvis X-Ray — Systematic Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Trauma, groin/hip pain, AVN risk factors, metastases, THA follow-up
  • 2
    Views
    • AP pelvis, cross-table lateral, frog-leg lateral, Judet views (acetabular fractures)
  • 3
    Pelvic Ring & Acetabulum
    • Iliopectineal and ilioischial lines: intact
    • SI joints: width ≤4 mm symmetric
    • Pubic symphysis: width ≤5 mm, vertical alignment ≤2 mm
    • Acetabular walls: anterior, posterior, roof integrity
  • 4
    Femoral Head & Neck
    • Sphericity of femoral head; subchondral crescent (AVN)
    • Femoral neck: Garden I–IV classification
    • Intertrochanteric: stable vs. unstable; subtrochanteric = pathologic until proven otherwise
  • 5
    Hip Joint Space
    • Normal 3–5 mm uniform; asymmetry >3 mm = effusion/septic arthritis
    • Superior narrowing: OA; uniform narrowing: RA/infection
  • 6
    Soft Tissue Fat Planes
    • Obturator fat stripe: obliterated = effusion/mass
    • Iliopsoas: calcification (bursitis)
  • 7
    Pelvic Avulsion Fractures (Athletes)
    • AIIS (rectus femoris), ASIS (sartorius), ischial tuberosity (hamstrings), lesser trochanter (iliopsoas — pathologic in adults)
  • 8
    Pediatric Hip
    • LCP (4–10 yr): femoral head sclerosis/fragmentation, lateral subluxation
    • SCFE (10–15 yr): posterior-inferior slip; Klein's line disrupted
    • DDH: acetabular index >30°; Shenton's line disrupted
  • 9
    Bone Lesions
    • Proximal femur: metastases, NOF, enchondroma
    • Pelvis: Paget (expanded, coarsened trabeculae)
  • 10
    THA (if post-op)
    • Cup: 40–45° abduction, 15–20° anteversion
    • Stem: parallel to canal, no subsidence
    • Lucency >2 mm at hardware-bone interface = loosening
  • 11
    Last Checks
    • Bone windows for subtle lytic lesions
    • Sacral foramina symmetry
    • Bowel gas on pelvic portion
  • 12
    Bilateral Comparison
    • Joint space, femoral head sphericity, offset
    • Harris hip anatomy: head-neck offset, center-edge angle
⚠ Elderly + hip pain + negative XR → MRI within 24–48 h to exclude occult femoral neck fracture.
Knee X-Ray XR
Knee X-Ray — Systematic Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Trauma (Ottawa Knee Rules), effusion, locking, instability, pain, post-op
  • 2
    Views
    • AP standing (weight-bearing), lateral, tunnel/notch (Rosenberg), Merchant/sunrise
  • 3
    Alignment
    • Tibiofemoral angle: normal slight valgus 5–7°; varus (OA) or valgus
    • Patellar height: Insall-Salvati ratio >1.3 = alta, <0.8 = baja
  • 4
    Distal Femur
    • Condylar fractures: medial, lateral, bicondylar
    • OCD: anterolateral medial femoral condyle (most common)
  • 5
    Proximal Tibia
    • Tibial plateau: Schatzker I–VI; depression >5 mm = significant
    • Cortical disruption, Salter-Harris (pediatric)
  • 6
    Fibula Head
    • Arcuate fracture (posterolateral corner injury)
    • Segond fracture: lateral tibial rim avulsion (ACL tear pathognomonic)
  • 7
    Patella
    • Bipartite: superolateral, smooth margins vs. acute fracture
    • Patellar fracture: transverse (most common), stellate
    • Subluxation on sunrise view
  • 8
    Joint Space & Articular Surfaces
    • Medial vs. lateral compartment (standing AP): OA (asymmetric), RA (diffuse)
    • CPPD: meniscal or articular cartilage calcification
  • 9
    Effusion (Lateral View)
    • Suprapatellar bursa >5 mm = effusion
    • Lipohemarthrosis: fat-fluid level = intraarticular fracture
  • 10
    Soft Tissues & Calcifications
    • Pellegrini-Stieda: medial condyle ossification (MCL injury)
    • Loose bodies: calcified intraarticular fragments
⚠ Lipohemarthrosis on lateral = intraarticular fracture — search all osseous structures carefully.
Ankle X-Ray XR
Ankle X-Ray — Systematic Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Mechanism: inversion (lateral ligaments), eversion (deltoid), axial load (pilon); Ottawa Ankle Rules
  • 2
    Views
    • AP, mortise (15–20° internal rotation), lateral
  • 3
    Mortise Alignment
    • Uniform joint space ≤3 mm medial, superior, lateral
    • Fibular length: distal fibula at tibial plafond level
    • Talar tilt: any = significant
    • Medial clear space ≤4 mm
  • 4
    Distal Fibula & Lateral Malleolus
    • Weber/Danis: A (below), B (at — most common), C (above syndesmosis)
  • 5
    Medial Malleolus
    • Horizontal (avulsion) vs. vertical (compression) fracture pattern
  • 6
    Posterior Malleolus (Lateral View)
    • Fracture >25% articular surface = surgical fixation
  • 7
    Syndesmosis
    • Tibiofibular clear space >5 mm = disrupted
    • Tibiofibular overlap: ≥10 mm on AP; ≥1 mm on mortise
  • 8
    Calcaneus
    • Böhler's angle: normal 25–40°; reduced = calcaneal fracture
  • 9
    Tarsal Bones
    • Talar neck (Hawkins I–III); lateral process (snowboarder); dome OCD
    • Hawkins sign at 6–8 wk = vascularity preserved
    • 5th MT base: Jones fracture (diaphyseal) vs. avulsion (tuberosity)
    • Lisfranc: 1st MT–medial cuneiform alignment; >2 mm diastasis between 1st and 2nd MT base
Foot X-Ray XR
Foot X-Ray — Systematic Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Trauma (mechanism, weight-bearing status), chronic pain, diabetic foot, deformity
  • 2
    Views
    • AP, oblique, lateral (weight-bearing for deformity)
  • 3
    Alignment
    • Meary angle: talo-1st MT axis (sag = pes planus; elevated = pes cavus)
  • 4
    Lisfranc Joint
    • 2nd MT base aligns with medial border of middle cuneiform
    • Diastasis >2 mm between 1st and 2nd MT base = Lisfranc injury
    • Fleck sign: avulsion at Lisfranc ligament
  • 5
    Metatarsals
    • Stress fracture: 2nd MT (march fracture) — lucent line + periosteal reaction
    • 5th MT: Jones (metadiaphyseal) vs. tuberosity avulsion
  • 6
    Tarsals
    • Navicular stress fracture (central 1/3)
    • Cuboid nutcracker fracture (forced abduction)
    • Accessory navicular: types I–III
  • 7
    Phalanges
    • Tuft fractures (distal)
    • 1st MTP sesamoids: fracture vs. bipartite (smooth sclerotic margins)
    • Hallux valgus: HV angle >15°; intermetatarsal angle >9°
  • 8
    Joint Spaces
    • 1st MTP: hallux rigidus (dorsal osteophyte), gout (eccentric erosions)
    • MCP/PIP: RA erosions
  • 9
    Soft Tissues
    • Gas = necrotizing fasciitis (diabetic emergency)
    • Soft tissue swelling, foreign body
MRI Shoulder MRI
Standard: coronal PD fat-sat (rotator cuff), axial PD fat-sat (labrum), sagittal PD fat-sat (outlet/muscle bulk), T1 (marrow/fatty infiltration). MRA improves labral and partial tear detection.
MRI Anatomy & Variants Rotator Cuff Injury Instability Shoulder Ultrasound
MRI Shoulder — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Impingement vs. instability vs. rotator cuff tear vs. adhesive capsulitis
    • Overhead athlete vs. recreational vs. elderly (full-thickness more likely)
    • Prior X-ray, MRI, or arthroscopy
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: coronal PD fat-sat, axial PD/T2 fat-sat, sagittal PD fat-sat, T1; MRA sequences if arthrogram
    • Coverage: AC joint superiorly through axillary recess inferiorly
  • 3
    Coronal PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Rotator Cuff (Start Here)
    • Supraspinatus tendon: T2 bright linear = tear; intratendinous = partial tear; critical zone 1 cm proximal to footprint
    • Full-thickness tear: fluid signal traversing tendon; retraction distance; muscle atrophy (Goutallier grade)
    • Partial tear: articular surface (most common), bursal surface, or intrasubstance
    • Infraspinatus: posterior coronal slices
    • Subscapularis: anterior coronal slices
    • Subacromial-subdeltoid bursa: T2 bright fluid — bursitis
  • 4
    Axial PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Labrum & Biceps
    • Anterior labrum: Bankart (fibrocartilaginous or bony); ALPSA lesion
    • Posterior labrum: reverse Bankart, Bennett lesion (throwers)
    • SLAP tear: superior labrum types I–IV; biceps anchor
    • Biceps LHT: tenosynovitis (fluid in sheath), tear, empty groove (complete tear)
    • Subscapularis: medial dislocation of biceps tendon = subscapularis tear
    • Glenohumeral cartilage: anterior and posterior glenoid, humeral head
    • Capsule: IGHL, MGHL, SGHL; axillary recess loose bodies
  • 5
    Sagittal PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Outlet & Muscle Bulk
    • Acromion: type I/II/III, slope, inferior spur
    • Subacromial space <7 mm = impingement
    • Coracoacromial arch: CA ligament thickening
    • AC joint inferior spur impinging on supraspinatus
    • Rotator cuff muscle bulk: all four muscles — atrophy and fatty infiltration (Goutallier 0–4)
  • 6
    T1 — Marrow & Fatty Infiltration
    • Hill-Sachs: posterolateral humeral head cortical depression
    • Glenoid: bony Bankart (anterior rim osseous defect)
    • Fatty infiltration assessment: T1 best for Goutallier grading
    • Acromion and coracoid marrow: edema at impingement surfaces
  • 7
    MRA (if arthrogram)
    • Labral tears: intraarticular contrast extending into tear
    • Undersurface partial RTC tears: contrast enters articular side tendon
    • HAGL lesion: contrast extravasation at humeral IGHL attachment
    • Subscapularis tears: contrast in subcoracoid bursa
  • 8
    Extratarget
    • AC joint: OA, distal clavicle osteolysis
    • Lung apex: Pancoast tumor (shoulder pain + neurologic)
    • Cervical spine foraminal stenosis on superior cuts
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • Rotator interval: SGHL, coracohumeral ligament (adhesive capsulitis = T2 dark thickening)
    • Report: tear type, size, retraction, Goutallier grade
    • Compare with prior MRI or arthroscopy report
MRI Elbow MRI
Standard: coronal PD fat-sat (UCL, RCL, tendons), axial PD/T2 fat-sat (ulnar nerve, biceps/triceps), sagittal PD fat-sat (biceps, OCD capitellum). T1 for marrow. 3T preferred.
MRI Examination of the Elbow
MRI Elbow — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Medial (UCL, flexor-pronator, ulnar nerve) vs. lateral (RCL, ECRB, capitellum OCD) vs. anterior (biceps) vs. posterior (triceps)
    • Overhead throwing athlete or not
    • Prior MRI or X-ray
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: coronal PD fat-sat, axial T2/PD fat-sat, sagittal T2/PD fat-sat, T1
    • MRA improves partial UCL tear and loose body detection
    • Coverage: distal humerus through proximal forearm
  • 3
    Coronal PD/T2 Fat-Sat — UCL, RCL & Tendons (Start Here)
    • UCL anterior bundle: origin medial epicondyle → coronoid tubercle; T2 signal, T-sign (avulsion with deep fiber intact), complete discontinuity
    • RCL complex: LUCL (posterolateral stability), RCL, annular, accessory
    • Common extensor tendon origin (lateral epicondyle): T2 signal = lateral epicondylosis (tennis elbow)
    • Common flexor tendon origin (medial epicondyle): T2 signal = medial epicondylosis (golfer's elbow)
    • Capitellum OCD: anterolateral, articular cartilage integrity, loose body formation
    • Articular cartilage: ulnohumeral and radiocapitellar
  • 4
    Axial PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Ulnar Nerve & Other
    • Ulnar nerve: T2 signal (neuritis), cross-sectional area (>10 mm² = cubital tunnel syndrome), perineural thickening
    • Cubital tunnel retinaculum: intact vs. absent (nerve subluxation)
    • Biceps tendon: distal attachment at radial tuberosity (partial vs. complete tear)
    • Triceps tendon: olecranon attachment
    • Joint effusion: coronoid + olecranon fossae
    • Loose bodies: posterolateral, anterior joint
  • 5
    Sagittal PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Biceps & Triceps
    • Distal biceps: radial tuberosity attachment; biceps retinaculum (lacertus fibrosus)
    • Triceps: olecranon insertion; partial vs. complete tear
    • Capitellum OCD: depth, fragment, cartilage cap integrity
    • Trochlea: osteochondral integrity
  • 6
    T1 — Marrow
    • Lateral epicondyle: stress reaction (T1 dark edema)
    • Medial epicondyle: apophysitis in young throwers (Little League elbow)
    • Capitellum: OCD (T1 dark subchondral); Panner disease (children — diffuse osteonecrosis)
  • 7
    Extratarget
    • Proximal forearm compartment strains
    • Regional lymphadenopathy
    • Brachial artery
  • 8
    Last Checks
    • UCL all 3 bundles: anterior (primary), posterior, transverse
    • OCD: stable vs. unstable (intact cartilage vs. loose body)
    • Ulnar nerve size + signal for cubital tunnel report
MRI Wrist MRI
Standard: coronal PD fat-sat (TFCC, ligaments), coronal T1 (carpal marrow), axial T2 fat-sat (carpal tunnel, tendons). 3T with small-bore coil preferred. MRA improves TFCC and intrinsic ligament accuracy.
Carpal Instability
MRI Wrist — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Ulnar-sided pain (TFCC) vs. radial-sided (scaphoid, SL) vs. carpal tunnel (median nerve)
    • Mechanism: axial load, hyperdorsiflexion, twisting
    • Prior wrist X-ray or MRI
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: coronal PD fat-sat, coronal T1, axial T2/PD fat-sat, sagittal PD fat-sat
    • MRA for TFCC, SL, LT tears
    • Coverage: DRUJ through proximal metacarpals
  • 3
    Coronal PD/T2 Fat-Sat — TFCC & Ligaments (Start Here)
    • TFCC central disk: T2 dark = normal; T2 bright = Palmer 1A central tear
    • Peripheral foveal attachment (Palmer 1B): T2 signal at ulnar attachment = DRUJ instability
    • SL ligament: dorsal band (primary stabilizer); complete tear = gap on multiple planes
    • LT ligament: tear — LT gap; associated with VISI
    • Extrinsic ligaments: radioscaphocapitate, long and short radiolunate
    • DRUJ articular cartilage
  • 4
    Coronal T1 — Carpal Marrow
    • Scaphoid: fracture line (T1 dark), AVN proximal pole (T1 dark = Preiser)
    • Lunate: Kienböck disease — T1 dark (edema/early AVN); Stahl/Lichtman staging
    • Triquetrum: dorsal chip fracture (T1 dark)
    • Hamate: hook fracture (T1 dark at base)
    • All carpal bones: uniform marrow signal
  • 5
    Axial T2/PD Fat-Sat — Carpal Tunnel & Tendons
    • Median nerve: T2 signal (bright = neuritis), cross-sectional area >15 mm² = CTS, flattening ratio
    • Flexor tendons: tenosynovitis (T2 bright fluid in sheath), tendon signal
    • Flexor retinaculum: thickening (CTS)
    • Guyon canal: ulnar nerve and artery; ganglion compression
    • Extensor compartments I–VI: De Quervain (1st), tenosynovitis, tendon signal
    • Ganglion cysts: dorsal (SL ligament) or volar (radiocarpal)
  • 6
    Sagittal PD Fat-Sat — Alignment
    • Radius–lunate–capitate axis: DISI (dorsal lunate tilt) vs. VISI (palmar tilt)
    • SL and RL angles; scaphoid humpback deformity
  • 7
    Extratarget
    • Distal radius: fracture, DRUJ articular surface
    • Metacarpal bases: CMC fracture-dislocation
    • Thenar/hypothenar muscle signal
  • 8
    Last Checks
    • TFCC Palmer classification: traumatic 1A–1E
    • SL gap confirmation on multiple planes
    • Kienböck: Stahl/Lichtman stage for surgical planning
MRI Hip & Pelvis MRI
Standard: coronal T1 bilateral, coronal STIR/fat-sat, axial PD fat-sat. Radial sequences for FAI protocol. MRA significantly improves labral tear detection.
Femoroacetabular Impingement (FAI) Hip Arthroplasty
MRI Hip & Pelvis — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Groin (labrum, FAI, chondral) vs. lateral (gluteal tendinopathy, trochanteric bursitis) vs. posterior (hamstring, SI)
    • AVN risk factors (steroids, alcohol, sickle cell, trauma); FAI in young athlete
    • Prior hip X-ray or MRI
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: coronal T1 bilateral, coronal STIR/fat-sat, axial PD fat-sat; ± radial sequences (FAI)
    • MRA (direct) for labral tears and cartilage
    • Coverage: iliac crest through lesser trochanters bilaterally
  • 3
    Coronal T1 — Bone Marrow & Bilateral Anatomy (Start Here)
    • Femoral head and neck marrow: normal T1 bright fat; T1 dark = edema, metastasis, osteonecrosis
    • AVN band: T1 dark subchondral signal at weight-bearing zone; double-line sign on T2 = pathognomonic
    • Femoral neck fracture: T1 dark fracture line; complete vs. incomplete
    • Greater trochanter marrow; gluteal tendon footprint
    • Bilateral symmetry comparison
  • 4
    Coronal STIR / Fat-Sat — Edema & Soft Tissue
    • Bone marrow edema: transient osteoporosis (diffuse T2 bright = TOH), stress fracture (T2 bright + fracture line), AVN surrounding reactive edema
    • Labral signal: T2 bright tear at labral base; superior and anterior labrum most vulnerable
    • Gluteus medius and minimus tendons: T2 bright = tendinosis; full-thickness tear (abductor mechanism)
    • Trochanteric bursa: T2 bright fluid = bursitis
    • Iliopsoas bursa, sartorius/rectus femoris avulsion
    • Sacrum and SI joints: edema
  • 5
    Axial PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Labrum & Cartilage
    • Labrum: anterior (3–5 o'clock), posterior (7–9 o'clock), superior (12 o'clock — most important)
    • Paralabral cyst + labral T2 signal = tear
    • Cam morphology: alpha angle >55° at 3 o'clock = cam FAI
    • Acetabular and femoral head cartilage: focal defects, thinning
    • Hip capsule: thickening (adhesive capsulitis); iliofemoral ligament
    • Sciatic nerve: signal and diameter
  • 6
    Radial Sequences (if FAI)
    • Circumferential labrum assessment at each clock position
    • Alpha angle at 12, 1, 2, 3 o'clock
    • Cam (femoral-side bump) vs. pincer (acetabular overcoverage) vs. combined
  • 7
    T1+C / MRA (if performed)
    • Labral tears: contrast into labral substance or paralabral recess
    • Cartilage: smooth coating of femoral head and acetabulum
    • Synovitis: thickened enhancing synovium; loose bodies
  • 8
    Extratarget
    • SI joints bilaterally: active sacroiliitis (T2/STIR subchondral marrow edema + erosions)
    • Pubic symphysis: osteitis pubis edema
    • Proximal hamstrings: ischial avulsion, tendinopathy
    • Lower lumbar spine on sagittal images
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • AVN: Ficat/Steinberg staging if applicable
    • Alpha angle at 3 o'clock for cam FAI
    • Labral tear: clock face location, partial vs. complete
    • Abductor mechanism: Goutallier-equivalent for gluteal fatty infiltration
MRI Knee MRI
Standard: sagittal PD fat-sat, coronal PD fat-sat, axial PD fat-sat, sagittal T1, coronal T1. 3T preferred. Arthrogram for post-meniscectomy or subtle chondral lesions.
Meniscal Pathology Non-Meniscal Pathology (ACL/PCL/MCL/PLC) Meniscus — Special Cases
MRI Knee — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Mechanism: ACL (valgus + external rotation), PCL (posterior force flexed knee), meniscus (twisting), MCL (valgus stress), LCL (varus)
    • Acute swelling vs. chronic pain/locking vs. instability
    • Prior MRI or arthroscopy
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: sagittal PD fat-sat, coronal PD fat-sat, axial PD fat-sat, sagittal T1, coronal T1
    • Coverage: distal femur through proximal tibia; fibular head included
  • 3
    Sagittal PD/T2 Fat-Sat — ACL, PCL, Posterior Menisci, Tendons
    • ACL: fiber continuity, T2 signal, course (normally taut 45–55°); complete tear = discontinuity, horizontal course, mass-like hematoma
    • Indirect ACL signs: posterior tibial translation, deep lateral sulcus sign, pivot shift bone marrow edema (lateral femoral condyle + posterior lateral tibial plateau)
    • PCL: normally curvilinear, dark; complete tear = T2 bright, fiber discontinuity
    • Posterior horn menisci: signal grade I–III; III = surface-communicating = tear
    • Patellar and quadriceps tendons: thickness, T2 signal (tendinosis, Sinding-Larsen, Osgood-Schlatter)
    • Hoffa fat pad: T2 signal (impingement)
  • 4
    Coronal PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Collateral Ligaments, Menisci, Compartments
    • MCL: superficial and deep layers; complete vs. partial; site (femoral origin most common)
    • Posterolateral corner (PLC): LCL, popliteus tendon, popliteofibular ligament; arcuate fracture on XR
    • Medial meniscus body and root: root tear = pseudo-bucket handle + medial extrusion
    • Lateral meniscus: discoid (large body covering entire plateau)
    • Bone marrow edema pattern: mechanism-specific — lateral condyle/tibial plateau = pivot shift; medial = valgus
    • Cartilage: medial and lateral compartment, full-thickness defects
    • IT band: T2 bright (IT band syndrome)
  • 5
    Axial PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Patellofemoral
    • Trochlear dysplasia: Dejour classification; sulcus angle, trochlear depth
    • Patellar tilt and subluxation: lateral retinaculum thickening
    • MPFL: T2 bright or discontinuity = tear (patellar dislocation injury)
    • Patellar cartilage: medial facet (first in lateral dislocation), lateral, odd facet
    • Prepatellar and infrapatellar bursae: fluid
  • 6
    T1 — Bone Marrow & Contusion Pattern
    • Pivot shift: lateral femoral condyle posterior + posterior lateral tibial plateau
    • Dashboard (PCL): anterior proximal tibia
    • Valgus (MCL): medial femoral condyle + lateral tibial plateau
    • Subchondral fracture: OCD, SONK
    • Salter-Harris in pediatric
  • 7
    Meniscal Assessment (All Sequences)
    • Signal grade: grade III = surface-communicating tear
    • Tear patterns: horizontal cleavage, radial, vertical longitudinal, oblique, root
    • Bucket-handle: absent bow-tie sign; double PCL sign on sagittal
    • Root tears: posterior root medial meniscus = extrusion + accelerated OA
    • Extrusion: >3 mm lateral displacement = significant
    • Parameniscal cysts: indicates underlying tear
  • 8
    Extratarget
    • Proximal tibiofibular joint
    • Popliteal fossa: Baker cyst, popliteal artery, mass
    • Fibular head: arcuate fracture (PLC injury)
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • ACL: complete vs. partial; remnant tissue for partial repair
    • Meniscal tears: type, location (zone), root vs. non-root
    • MPFL + patellar cartilage: document for instability workup
    • Compare with prior: new vs. old chondral, healed vs. persistent tear
MRI Ankle & Hindfoot MRI
Standard: coronal PD fat-sat (lateral/medial ligaments, peroneals), axial PD/T2 fat-sat (posterior tibial tendon, Achilles, tarsal tunnel), sagittal T2/PD fat-sat (Achilles, impingement), coronal T1 (bone marrow).
MRI Examination of the Ankle
MRI Ankle — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Lateral instability (ATFL/CFL) vs. medial (PTT, deltoid) vs. posterior (Achilles, FHL, os trigonum) vs. anterior impingement
    • Chronic vs. acute; prior surgery; athlete vs. sedentary
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: coronal PD fat-sat, axial T2/PD fat-sat, sagittal T2/PD fat-sat, coronal T1
    • Coverage: distal tibia/fibula through calcaneus; all tarsal bones
    • Neutral foot position preferred
  • 3
    Coronal PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Lateral Ligaments & Peroneals (Start Here)
    • ATFL: fibular tip → talar neck; T2 bright, waviness, discontinuity = tear (most commonly torn ankle ligament)
    • CFL: fibular tip → lateral calcaneus; deep to peroneal tendons
    • PTFL: posterolateral, rarely torn
    • Peroneal tendons (PL and PB): split tear PB (longitudinal, most common), PL tear; tenosynovitis (T2 bright fluid in sheath)
    • Peroneal tendon dislocation: tendons anterior to fibula = SPR tear
    • Sinus tarsi: fat signal normal; T2 bright edema = sinus tarsi syndrome
    • AITFL and PITFL: syndesmosis assessment on coronal
  • 4
    Axial PD/T2 Fat-Sat — Medial Tendons, Tarsal Tunnel & Achilles Cross-Section
    • PTT (most anterior medial tendon): degeneration/tear (T2 bright intratendinous, thickening or caliber loss), navicular insertion
    • FDL: posterior to PTT
    • FHL: most posterior medial; tenosynovitis at posterior ankle (os trigonum syndrome)
    • Achilles tendon cross-section: intratendinous T2 signal, calcification
    • Tarsal tunnel: tibial nerve + medial/lateral plantar nerves; ganglion, space-occupying lesion
    • Deltoid ligament: deep (tibiotalocalcaneal) and superficial components
  • 5
    Sagittal T2/PD Fat-Sat — Achilles, Anterior & Posterior Impingement
    • Achilles mid-substance: T2 bright intratendinous signal, thickening 2–6 cm above insertion = tendinosis/tear
    • Insertional Achilles: irregular calcaneal attachment, Haglund deformity (posterior calcaneal spur), retrocalcaneal bursitis
    • Anterior impingement: anterior tibial / talar neck osteophytes; soft tissue fibrosis/synovitis
    • Posterior impingement: os trigonum or large Sternberg process; FHL tenosynovitis
    • Plantar fascia: T2 bright at calcaneal origin = plantar fasciitis; discontinuity = tear
    • Spring ligament: calcaneonavicular; tear with PTT dysfunction
  • 6
    Coronal T1 — Bone Marrow
    • Talar dome OCD: anterolateral (traumatic) vs. posteromedial (atraumatic); T1 dark subchondral change; stability assessment
    • Talus: AVN (T1 dark patchy marrow, body segment most vulnerable)
    • Calcaneus: stress fracture (T1 dark perpendicular line), sinus tarsi
    • Navicular: stress fracture (central 1/3), accessory navicular synchondrosis
    • All tarsal bones: marrow signal
  • 7
    Joint Assessment
    • Tibiotalar cartilage: anteromedial, posterolateral OA distribution
    • Subtalar posterior facet: cartilage, coalition (middle facet on axial — calcaneonavicular vs. talocalcaneal)
    • Talonavicular: cartilage, alignment
    • Joint effusion: T2 bright fluid
  • 8
    Extratarget
    • Distal tibia/fibula on superior slices: stress fracture
    • Syndesmosis integrity (AITFL/PITFL)
    • Midfoot on inferior slices: Lisfranc
    • Plantar intrinsic muscles: edema, Morton neuroma interspace
  • 9
    Last Checks
    • PTT: Johnson-Strom grade I–III (tenosynovitis → partial → complete)
    • OCD talar dome: stability (fluid underneath fragment = unstable)
    • Insertional vs. mid-substance Achilles: surgical approach differs
    • Peroneal: PB vs. PL distinction; dislocation noted
MSK MRI — Infection / Osteomyelitis MRI
T1 marrow replacement + STIR edema = osteomyelitis. T1+C fat-sat essential to distinguish abscess (rim-enhancing) from phlegmon (diffuse). DWI can identify abscess when T1+C limited.
Diabetic Foot — MRI Examination
MSK MRI — Infection / Osteomyelitis — Sequence-Based Review
  • 1
    History & Indication
    • Diabetes, immunocompromise, IV drug use, prior hardware, open wound, post-surgery
    • Fever, elevated WBC/ESR/CRP, bacteremia
    • Site: diabetic foot/ankle, spine (diskitis-osteomyelitis), post-op joint, hematogenous osteomyelitis in child (metaphysis)
  • 2
    Adequacy
    • Sequences: STIR or T2 fat-sat (coronal + axial), T1 (coronal + axial), T1 fat-sat post-contrast (coronal + axial)
    • Coverage: entire involved region + adjacent joints + proximal extent (surgical planning)
    • DWI if abscess suspected; note metallic hardware artifact limitation
  • 3
    T2 / STIR — Extent of Edema (Start Here)
    • Bone marrow edema: T2/STIR bright; single bone vs. multi-bone vs. contiguous spread from joint
    • Joint effusion: T2 bright fluid + thickened T2 bright synovium = septic arthritis
    • Soft tissue edema: diffuse (cellulitis) vs. compartmentalized (early abscess)
    • Fascial plane edema: compartment-by-compartment spread; multi-compartmental = necrotizing fasciitis pattern
    • Sinus tract: T2 bright linear channel through soft tissues to bone
    • Tenosynovitis in tendon sheaths; flexor tendons in diabetic foot
  • 4
    T1 — Marrow Signal (Critical for Osteomyelitis)
    • Normal marrow: T1 bright fat throughout
    • Osteomyelitis: focal T1 dark marrow replacement — most sensitive criterion (requires STIR correlation)
    • Extent: metaphysis, diaphysis, epiphysis
    • Cortical disruption: loss of hypointense cortical line
    • Sequestrum: T1 dark devascularized bone fragment
    • Involucrum: reactive new bone around sequestrum
  • 5
    T1 Fat-Sat Post-Contrast — Abscess vs. Phlegmon
    • Abscess: rim-enhancing fluid collection — thick irregular wall, non-enhancing T2 bright center
    • Phlegmon: diffuse heterogeneous enhancement without discrete fluid collection
    • Subperiosteal abscess: rim-enhancing between periosteum and cortex
    • Brodie's abscess: round T2 bright, rim enhancement, Penumbra sign (inner T1 bright granulation + outer dark sclerosis)
    • Sinus tract: enhancing tract from bone to skin
    • Necrotizing fasciitis: minimal fascial enhancement (ischemic fascia) + gas on CT
    • Septic arthritis: thick enhancing synovium, cartilage destruction
  • 6
    DWI / ADC (if performed)
    • Abscess: restricted diffusion (high cellularity, viscous pus)
    • Phlegmon: less restricted than abscess
    • Epidural abscess (spine): restricted diffusion of epidural collection
  • 7
    Hardware Assessment (if present)
    • Metal artifact reduction (MARS/MAVRIC/SEMAC) if available
    • Periimplant T2 halo: expected vs. pathologic (thickened)
    • Loosening vs. infection: loosening = T1 dark interface >2 mm; infection = periimplant enhancement + soft tissue involvement
    • Sinus tracts to hardware surface
  • 8
    Anatomic Extent & Surgical Planning
    • Compartmental involvement: which compartment? (surgical drainage)
    • Neurovascular proximity: artery, vein, nerve within infected zone
    • Proximal extent for debridement planning
    • Joint space involvement (septic arthritis — cartilage destruction)
    • Bone viability: dead bone = no enhancement (sequestrum)
  • 9
    Extratarget
    • Adjacent joint involvement
    • Proximal regional lymph nodes
    • Vascular structures: arteritis, pseudoaneurysm
  • 10
    Last Checks
    • Multi-compartment = necrotizing fasciitis? (surgical emergency)
    • Spine: epidural abscess extent and cord compression level
    • Diskitis-osteomyelitis: end plate enhancement + disk enhancement + STIR bright = classic triad
    • Compare with prior MRI for response to treatment
⚠ Necrotizing fasciitis: clinical diagnosis + imaging. Gas on CT is hallmark. MRI should NOT delay surgical debridement in critically ill patient.
